# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

**Target Repository:** `github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c`
- Use `repo:^github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c$` filter in keyword_search
- Use `github.com/sg-evals/django--674eda1c` as the `repo` parameter for go_to_definition/find_references/read_file


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

# Task: Implement RateLimitMiddleware for Django

## Objective
Create a new `RateLimitMiddleware` class in `django/middleware/ratelimit.py` that provides
configurable per-IP request rate limiting using Django's cache framework.

## Requirements

1. **Create `django/middleware/ratelimit.py`** with a `RateLimitMiddleware` class that:
   - Inherits from `MiddlewareMixin` (see `django/utils/deprecation.py`)
   - Reads configuration from `settings.RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS` (default: 100) and `settings.RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW` (default: 3600 seconds)
   - Uses Django's cache framework (`django.core.cache.cache`) to track request counts per IP
   - Returns `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` (429) when limit is exceeded
   - Implements `process_request(self, request)` following the middleware pattern

2. **Update `django/http/__init__.py`** to export `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` if not already present

3. **Create `tests/middleware/test_ratelimit.py`** with test cases for:
   - Normal requests within limit
   - Requests exceeding limit
   - Cache key isolation per IP
   - Custom settings override

## Key Reference Files
- `django/middleware/csrf.py` — middleware pattern with `process_request`/`process_view`
- `django/middleware/common.py` — middleware using settings and returning responses
- `django/utils/deprecation.py` — `MiddlewareMixin` base class
- `django/core/cache/__init__.py` — cache framework API
- `django/http/response.py` — HTTP response classes (HttpResponseForbidden, etc.)

## Success Criteria
- RateLimitMiddleware class exists and follows Django middleware conventions
- Uses cache framework for rate tracking (not in-memory dict)
- Returns 429 status code when rate limit exceeded
- Has proper imports from django.conf, django.core.cache, django.http
- Test file exists with JUnit-style test methods

   705→
   706→    def __init__(self, permitted_methods, *args, **kwargs):
   707→        super().__init__(*args, **kwargs)
   708→        self["Allow"] = ", ".join(permitted_methods)
   709→
   710→    def __repr__(self):
   711→        return "<%(cls)s [%(methods)s] status_code=%(status_code)d%(content_type)s>" % {
   712→            "cls": self.__class__.__name__,
   713→            "status_code": self.status_code,
   714→            "content_type": self._content_type_for_repr,
   715→            "methods": self["Allow"],
   716→        }

     1→from django.conf import settings
     2→from django.core.cache import cache
     3→from django.http import HttpResponseTooManyRequests
     4→from django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin
     5→
     6→
     7→class RateLimitMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):
     8→    """
     9→    Middleware to implement per-IP request rate limiting using Django's cache framework.
    10→
    11→    Configuration:
    12→    - RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS: Maximum number of requests per IP (default: 100)
    13→    - RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)
    14→    """
    15→
    16→    def process_request(self, request):
    17→        """
    18→        Check if the client IP has exceeded the rate limit.
    19→        Returns a 429 (Too Many Requests) response if limit is exceeded.
    20→        """
    21→        # Get configuration from settings with defaults
    22→        rate_limit_requests = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS', 100)
    23→        rate_limit_window = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW', 3600)
    24→
    25→        # Get client IP address
    26→        client_ip = request.META.get('REMOTE_ADDR', '')
    27→
    28→        # Create cache key unique to this IP
    29→        cache_key = f'ratelimit:{client_ip}'
    30→
    31→        # Get current request count for this IP
    32→        request_count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)
    33→
    34→        # Check if limit is exceeded
    35→        if request_count >= rate_limit_requests:
    36→            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests('Rate limit exceeded')
    37→
    38→        # Increment request count
    39→        cache.set(cache_key, request_count + 1, rate_limit_window)
    40→
    41→        return None
    42→

160-assistanttext-
Excellent! I've successfully implemented the RateLimitMiddleware for Django. Here's a summary of what was created:

## Implementation Summary

### 1. **HttpResponseTooManyRequests** (`django/http/response.py`)
- Added new HTTP response class with status code 429
- Follows Django's pattern for simple HTTP response classes

### 2. **Updated Exports** (`django/http/__init__.py`)
- Added `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` to imports
- Added to `__all__` list for public API

### 3. **RateLimitMiddleware** (`django/middleware/ratelimit.py`)
The middleware implements per-IP request rate limiting with:
- **Inheritance**: Extends `MiddlewareMixin` following Django conventions
- **Configuration**: Reads from settings with sensible defaults:
  - `RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS`: Max requests per IP (default: 100)
  - `RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW`: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)
- **Storage**: Uses Django's cache framework (`django.core.cache.cache`)
- **IP Tracking**: Creates unique cache keys per IP address (`ratelimit:{ip}`)
- **Response**: Returns 429 status when limit exceeded
- **Pattern**: Implements `process_request()` method returning:
  - `None` to allow request processing (request count within limit)
  - `HttpResponseTooManyRequests` to block request (limit exceeded)

### 4. **Comprehensive Tests** (`tests/middleware/test_ratelimit.py`)
Five test cases covering:
- ✅ Normal requests within limit (requests pass through)
- ✅ Requests exceeding limit (returns 429 status)
- ✅ Cache key isolation per IP (each IP has separate counter)
- ✅ Custom settings override (respects RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS and RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW)
- ✅ Missing REMOTE_ADDR edge case (handles gracefully with empty string default)

## Key Features

- **Cache-based**: No in-memory dictionaries, uses Django's configurable cache backe

To apply to a staticmethod or classmethod,\n113:     use @deprecate_posargs after @staticmethod or @classmethod.\n114: \n115:     Example: to deprecate passing option1 or option2 as posargs, change::\n116: \n117:         def some_func(request, option1, option2=True):\n118:             ...\n119: \n120:     to::\n121: \n122:         @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n123:         def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n124:             ...\n125: \n126:     After the deprecation period, remove the decorator (but keep the ``*``)::\n127: \n128:         def some_func(request, *, option1, option2=True):\n129:             ...\n130: \n131:     Caution: during the deprecation period, do not add any new *positional*\n132:     parameters or change the remaining ones. For example, this attempt to add a\n133:     new param would break code using the deprecated posargs::\n134: \n135:         @deprecate_posargs(RemovedInDjangoXXWarning, [\"option1\", \"option2\"])\n136:         def some_func(request, wrong_new_param=None, *, option1, option2=True):\n137:             # Broken: existing code may pass a value intended as option1 in the\n138:             # wrong_new_param position.\n139:             ...\n140: \n141:     However, it's acceptable to add new *keyword-only* parameters and to\n142:     re-order the existing ones, so long as the list passed to\n143:     @deprecate_posargs is kept in the original posargs order. Clear cache before each test\n        cache.clear()\n\n    def tearDown(self):\n        # Clear cache after each test\n        cache.clear()\n\n    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=2, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)\n    def test_normal_requests_within_limit(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Requests within the rate limit should pass through normally.\n        \"\"\"\n        middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response_ok)\n\n        # Create requests from the same IP\n        request1 = self.rf.get('/')\n        request1.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'\n\n        request2 = self.rf.get('/')\n        request2.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'\n\n        # Create multiple requests from the same IP\n        request1 = self.rf.get('/')\n        request1.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'\n\n        request2 = self.rf.get('/')\n        request2.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'\n\n        request3 = self.rf.get('/')\n        request3.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'\n\n        # First two should be allowed\n        response1 = middleware.process_request(request1)\n        response2 = middleware.process_request(request2)\n\n        self.assertIsNone(response1)\n        self.assertIsNone(response2)\n\n        # Third should be rejected\n        response3 = middleware.process_request(request3)\n\n        self.assertIsNotNone(response3)\n        self.assertEqual(response3.status_code, 429)\n\n    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=1, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)\n    def test_cache_key_isolation_per_ip(self):\n        \"\"\"\n        Each IP should have its own rate limit counter.\n        \"\"\"\n        middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response_ok)\n\n        # Create requests from different IPs\n        request1 = self.rf.get('/')\n        request1.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '192.168.1.1'\n\n        request2 = self.rf.get('/')\n        request2.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '192.168.1.2'\n\n        # First request from each IP should be allowed\n        response1 = middleware.process_request(request1)\n        response2 = middleware.process_request(request2)\n\n        self.assertIsNone(response1)\n        self.assertIsNone(response2)\n\n        # 4. WRITE /workspace/django/middleware/ratelimit.py
from django.conf import settings
from django.core.cache import cache
from django.http import HttpResponseTooManyRequests
from django.utils.deprecation import MiddlewareMixin


class RateLimitMiddleware(MiddlewareMixin):
    """
    Middleware to implement per-IP request rate limiting using Django's cache framework.

    Configuration:
    - RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS: Maximum number of requests per IP (default: 100)
    - RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW: Time window in seconds (default: 3600)
    """

    def process_request(self, request):
        """
        Check if the client IP has exceeded the rate limit.
        Returns a 429 (Too Many Requests) response if limit is exceeded.
        """
        # Get configuration from settings with defaults
        rate_limit_requests = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS', 100)
        rate_limit_window = getattr(settings, 'RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW', 3600)

        # Get client IP address
        client_ip = request.META.get('REMOTE_ADDR', '')

        # Create cache key unique to this IP
        cache_key = f'ratelimit:{client_ip}'

        # Get current request count for this IP
        request_count = cache.get(cache_key, 0)

        # Check if limit is exceeded
        if request_count >= rate_limit_requests:
            return HttpResponseTooManyRequests('Rate limit exceeded')

        # Increment request count
        cache.set(cache_key, request_count + 1, rate_limit_window)

        return None

5. WRITE /workspace/tests/middleware/test_ratelimit.py
from django.core.cache import cache
from django.http import HttpResponse, HttpResponseTooManyRequests
from django.middleware.ratelimit import RateLimitMiddleware
from django.test import RequestFactory, SimpleTestCase, override_settings


def get_response_ok(request):
    return HttpResponse("OK")


class RateLimitMiddlewareTest(SimpleTestCase):
    rf = RequestFactory()

    def setUp(self):
        # Clear cache before each test
        cache.clear()

    def tearDown(self):
        # Clear cache after each test
        cache.clear()

    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=2, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)
    def test_normal_requests_within_limit(self):
        """
        Requests within the rate limit should pass through normally.
        """
        middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response_ok)

        # Create requests from the same IP
        request1 = self.rf.get('/')
        request1.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'

        request2 = self.rf.get('/')
        request2.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'

        # Both requests should return None from process_request (allowing normal processing)
        response1 = middleware.process_request(request1)
        response2 = middleware.process_request(request2)

        self.assertIsNone(response1)
        self.assertIsNone(response2)

    @override_settings(RATE_LIMIT_REQUESTS=2, RATE_LIMIT_WINDOW=3600)
    def test_requests_exceeding_limit(self):
        """
        Requests exceeding the rate limit should return 429 Too Many Requests.
        """
        middleware = RateLimitMiddleware(get_response_ok)

        # Create multiple requests from the same IP
        request1 = self.rf.get('/')
        request1.META['REMOTE_ADDR'] = '127.0.0.1'

        request2 = self.rf.get('/')
        request2.META['REMOTE_AD
... (truncated)
